If a third party destroys it, the mortgagee is the claimant for compensation, takes the value, and it becomes a pledge in his hand because he is more entitled to the property when it exists, so likewise to what stands in its place. The compensation is the value on the day of destruction. If its value on destruction was 500 and on the day of pledge 1000, the third party pays 500, which becomes the pledge, and 500 of the debt is discharged. Commentary explains: the mortgagee claims because he has the prior right. The value at destruction is taken. Then the ruling for the additional 500 (difference between original and current value) is that it is considered destroyed by calamity. The consideration in pledge liability is value at possession, not at redemption. If the pledge is destroyed in the mortgagee's hands, the debt is reduced by the value. If only half is destroyed due to receipt of compensation, the mortgagee's liability remains for the other half. A final question asks why the mortgagee is not liable for decrease in value without destruction; the author answers that liability only arises at destruction.
Source pages p. 294

Commentary
This passage covers the ruling when a third party destroys the pledged property. The mortgagee is the one entitled to claim compensation from the third party, because his right to the property itself gives him the right to its substitute. The compensation is measured by the value on the day of destruction, not the day of pledging. The text gives an example: if the property was worth 1000 when pledged and only 500 when destroyed, the third party pays 500, which becomes the new pledge, and the debt reduces by 500. The remaining 500 (the loss in value) is considered as if destroyed by an act of God (āfa), and the mortgagee is not liable for it. The general principle stated is that in pledge liability, the value at the time of possession (qabḍ) is what matters, not the value at redemption. If the property is destroyed in the mortgagee's hands, the debt is reduced by its value. The passage ends with a question about decrease without destruction, and the answer is that liability only becomes settled at the time of destruction.

Key Terms
اجنبی (ajnabi): A third party who is neither the pledgor nor the mortgagee.
خصم (khasm): The litigant or party entitled to claim; here the mortgagee is the claimant against the third party.
قبض استیفاء (qabd istifa'): Possession for the purpose of collecting the debt; the mortgagee's possession is of this type.
یوم ہلاکت (yawm halāk): The day on which the property is destroyed; used to determine the value for compensation.
آفت (āfa): A calamity or act of God; used to describe loss not caused by human action.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a third party destroys the pledged property, who is entitled to claim compensation?
A) The pledgor, because he is the owner.
B) The mortgagee, because he has the prior right to the property.
C) Both jointly.
D) The judge.

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee is entitled to claim compensation from a third party who destroys the pledged property, and the compensation becomes a new pledge, reducing the debt accordingly.

When a Stranger Destroys the Pawn: Calculating Compensation
Ruling on compensation amount for destroyed pawn

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the amount of compensation a stranger must pay when destroying a pawned item and apply the rule using an example.

Core Idea
Compensation for a destroyed pawn is based on its value on the day of destruction, not the day of pledge.

A pawn (marhun) is held by the mortgagee (murtahin) as security for a debt. If a third party destroys the pawn, he must compensate. But how much? The Hanafi school answers: the value on the day of destruction. This lesson unpacks the logic and the example from the text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the parties involved
Pinpoint the three parties: pledgor (rahin) – owner of the pawn, mortgagee (murtahin) – creditor holding the pawn, and stranger (ajnabi) – the destroyer. Understand their roles.
2
Understand the substitution principle
The compensation (tawan) takes the place of the destroyed pawn. Since the mortgagee had the right to hold the pawn, he now has the right to hold the compensation as a new pawn.
This is a key Hanafi concept: the substitute inherits the legal status of the original.
3
Determine the valuation date
The amount of compensation is the market value of the pawn on the day it was destroyed, not on the day it was pledged. This is the core ruling.
Example: If the pawn was worth 1000 at pledge but 500 at destruction, the stranger pays 500.
4
Apply the deduction to the debt
The compensation is held by the mortgagee as a new pawn. The debt is reduced by the same amount because the substitute replaces the pawn that secured that portion of the debt.
In the example, the debt drops from 1000 to 500, and the 500 compensation becomes the new security.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ہی تاوان کیوں وصول کریگا ؟
تو جواب دیا کہ اگر مرہون موجود ہوتا تو اس کا زیادہ حقدار مرتہن ہوتا ہے تو جو چیز مرہون کے قائم مقام ہے اس کو واپس لینے کا حقدار بھی مرتہن ہی ہو گا۔
اب سوال پیدا ہوا کہ اجنبی سے کتنا تا وان لیا جائے گا؟
تو اس کا جواب دیا کہ جس دن اجنبی نے مرہون کو ہلاک کیا اس دن جو مر ہون کی قیمت ہو اتنا تا وان اجنبی سے لیا جائے گا مثلاً رہن رکھنے کے دن مرہون کی قیمت ہزار روپیہ ہے اور قرض بھی اتفاق سے ہزار روپے ہے اور ہلاکت کے دن مرہون کی قیمت صرف پانچ سوروپے ہے تو اجنبی پر صرف پانچ سو کا تاوان واجب ہوگا ۔ اور یہ پانچ سوروپے مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہیں گے اور قرض میں سے پانچ سوروپے ساقط ہو گئے یعنی اب صرف راہن پر صرف پانچ سو روپیہ قرض رہا جن کا عوض اب یہ قیمت ہے جو مرتہن کے پاس رکھی گئی ہے۔
Why would he receive compensation? The answer was given that if the pawn existed, the mortgagee would be more entitled to it, so the one who takes the thing that stands in place of the pawn is also the mortgagee. Now a question arose: how much compensation will be taken from the stranger? The answer was given that on the day the stranger destroyed the pawn, whatever its value, that much compensation will be taken from the stranger. For example, on the day of pledging, the pawn's value is one thousand rupees, and the debt also happens to be one thousand rupees, and on the day of destruction, the pawn's value is only five hundred rupees, then the stranger is obligated only for five hundred rupees of compensation. And these five hundred rupees will remain with the mortgagee as a pawn, and five hundred rupees of the debt are dropped, meaning now only five hundred rupees of debt remain on the pledgor, and this value placed with the mortgagee is its substitute.
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on the scenario where a third party (ajnabi) destroys the pawned item (marhun). It first establishes that the compensation (tawan) takes the place of the pawn and belongs to the mortgagee (murtahin) as a new pawn. The key ruling is that the amount of compensation is determined by the value of the pawn on the day it was destroyed, not on the day it was pledged. An example illustrates: if the pawn was worth 1000 at pledge and 500 at destruction, the stranger pays 500. This 500 becomes a new pawn in the mortgagee's hands, and the debt is reduced by 500, leaving 500 owed. This is based on the principle that the mortgagee's right is attached to the pawn, and its substitute inherits that attachment.

Key Terms
مرہون (marhun): The item that is pledged as collateral for a debt.
مرتہن (murtahin): The creditor who receives the pawn as security for the debt.
تاوان (tawan): Compensation paid by a wrongdoer for destroying someone else's property.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a stranger destroys a pawned item that was worth 1000 at the time of pledge and 500 at destruction, how much compensation does the stranger pay?
A) 1000
B) 500
C) 1500
D) 0

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi ruling: the amount of compensation for a destroyed pawn is its market value on the day of destruction, and the compensation becomes a new pawn held by the mortgagee while the debt is reduced proportionally.

6 min
Liability for a Destroyed Pawn: Value at Receipt Principle
Ruling on debt reduction when pawn is destroyed in mortgagee's custody

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the basis for the mortgagee's liability when a pawn is destroyed and apply the rule to determine reduction of debt.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, the mortgagee's guarantee for a pawn is based on its value at receipt, and only becomes fixed upon destruction, not mere depreciation.

This lesson examines a key rule in the contract of rahn: when a pawn is destroyed in the mortgagee's custody, how does the debt adjust? The Hanafi school establishes that the mortgagee's liability rests on the value at the time the pawn was received, not at redemption, and that the guarantee crystallizes only if the pawn is actually destroyed. We will unpack the reasoning and the practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two time points
Recognize that the Hanafi ruling distinguishes between the value at receipt (qabd) and the value at redemption (fak). The guarantee is based on the former.
2
Understand the type of possession
The mortgagee's possession is 'qabd istifa'' (possession for collection), making him liable for the pawn from the moment of receipt, but the liability becomes concrete only at destruction.
Contrast with 'qabd amanah' where liability only arises with negligence.
3
Apply the principle of taqarrur 'inda al-halak
The guarantee is finalized at the time of destruction. Until then, mere decrease in value does not reduce the debt.
The phrase 'illa annahu yataqarraru bi al-halak' is key.
4
Distinguish actual destruction from price drop
A market fluctuation or price decrease without destruction does not trigger liability; the debt remains unchanged until redemption.
This prevents uncertainty in the security arrangement.
5
Apply to the example
In the case where the pawn's value dropped from 1000 to 500 due to a stranger's destruction, the additional 500 is treated as destroyed in the mortgagee's hands, reducing the debt to 500.
The stranger pays the value at destruction, but the mortgagee's liability is based on value at receipt.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اگر مرہون مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے تو کیا حکم ہے
فصار الحكم في الخمس مائة الزيادة كانها هلكت بآفة والمعتبر في ضمان الرهن القيمة يوم القبض لا يوم الفكاك لان القبض السابق مضمون عليه لأنه قبض الاستيفاء الا انه يتقرر عند الهلاك ترجمہ پس ہو جائے گا حکم ان پانچ سو میں جو زائد ہیں ( یعنی فی الحال کی قیمت سے جو زیادہ ہے ) گویا کہ وہ کسی آفت سے ہلاک ہوئے ہیں۔ اور ضمان رہن میں قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت معتبر سے نہ کہ چھڑانے کے دن کی اس لئے کہ سابق قبضہ مرتہن پر مضمون ہے اس لئے کہ یہ (مرتبہن کا قبضہ ) قبضہ استفاد ہے مگر ضمان ہلاکت کے وقت مقرر ہوتا ہے۔ تشریح اگر مرہون مرتہن کے پاس ہلاک ہو جائے خواہ مرتہن کے ہلاک کرنے سے یا کسی آسمانی آفت کی وجہ سے تو بقدر قیمت مرهون قرض ساقط ہو جاتا ہے ( کمامر )
تو یہاں اگر چہ پورا مرہون ہلاک نہیں ہوا بلکہ نصف ہلاک ہوا کیونکہ پانچ سوروپے مرتہن کو اجنبی سے مل گئے ہیں تو جتنا قیمت گھٹنے سے ہلاک ہوا ہے وہ ہلاکت یا گھٹی مرتہن کے ذمہ ہوگی لہذا یوں سمجھا جائے گا کہ مرتہن کے پاس پانچ سو کے بقدر ہلاک ہوا ہے تو اتنا ہی اس کا قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا کیونکہ اجنبی اگر ہلاک کرتا ہے تو اس پر یوم ہلاکت کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے جو اس نے دید یا مگر مرتبین پر قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت کا ضمان واجب ہوتا ہے چھڑانے کے دن کی قیمت کا اعتبار ہوتا ہے کیونکہ مرتہن کا قبضہ قبضہ استیفاء ہوتا ہے لہذا مرہون مرتہن کی زیر ضمانت بوقت رہن داخل ہو چکا ہے اور اب اس کی قیمت گھٹ کر آدھی رہ گئی تو باقی کا ضمان مرتہن پر باقی رہا اور اس کے بقدر مرتہن کا قرض ختم ہو کر پانچ سو باقی رہ گیا۔ سوال جب مرتہن پر قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت معتبر ہوتی ہے تو پھر ایسا ہونا چاہیے کہ اگر مرہون ہلاک نہ ہو اور مرتہن کے پاس اس کی قیمت گھٹ گئی تو قیمت کے نقصان کے بقدر قرض ہو جائے گا اور باقی قرض راہن ادا کر کے اپنے مرہون کو چھڑالے؟ جواب ... مصنف نے اس کا جواب الا انه يتصور :: الھلاک سے دیا ہے یعنی ابھی مرتہن پر اس گھٹی کا تاوان واجب نہ ہوگا
کیونکہ ضمان میں مضبوطی مرہون کی ہلاکت سے آتی ہے اور مرہون ہلاک نہیں ہوا بلکہ زندہ ہے صرف بھاؤ گھٹنے کی وجہ سے اس کی قیمت گھٹی ہے تو ابھی ضمان میں تقر رو پختگی نہیں آئی لہذا اسی حال میں اگر راہن اس کو چھڑائے گا تو پورا قرض دیکر چھڑائیگا اور صورتِ مبحوثہ میں چونکہ اجنبی کے پاس مرہون ہلاک ہو چکا ہے تو اب قبضہ کے دن کی پوری قیمت معتبر ہوگی ( کمامر )
If the pawn is destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, what is the ruling? The ruling becomes that the additional five hundred are as if destroyed by a calamity. And the consideration in the guarantee of the pawn is the value on the day of receipt, not the day of redemption, because the earlier receipt is guaranteed upon him because it is a receipt of fulfillment, but it is finalized at the time of destruction. Translation: So the ruling regarding those five hundred that are extra (i.e., more than the current value) becomes that they are as if destroyed by a calamity. And in the guarantee of the pawn, the value at the time of receipt is considered, not the day of redemption, because the earlier receipt is guaranteed upon the mortgagee because it is a receipt of fulfillment, but the guarantee is determined at the time of destruction. Explanation: If the pawn is destroyed in the mortgagee's possession, whether by his act or by a heavenly calamity, then the debt drops to the extent of the pawn's value (as mentioned). So here, although the entire pawn was not destroyed, rather half was destroyed because the mortgagee received five hundred rupees from the stranger, so whatever amount was destroyed due to the price decrease is considered destruction in the mortgagee's liability. Therefore, it will be understood that in the mortgagee's possession, five hundred worth was destroyed, so that much of his debt drops. Because when a stranger destroys, the guarantee for the value at the day of destruction is obligatory upon him, and he has paid it; but upon the mortgagee, the guarantee for the value at the day of receipt is obligatory, not the value at the day of redemption, because the mortgagee's possession is a possession of fulfillment. Hence, the pawn entered under the mortgagee's guarantee at the time of pledge, and now its value has decreased to half, so the guarantee for the remainder remains upon the mortgagee, and to that extent, the mortgagee's debt is extinguished, leaving five hundred. Question: Since the value at the day of receipt is considered for the mortgagee, then it should happen that if the pawn is not destroyed and its value decreases in the mortgagee's possession, then the debt should decrease by the amount of loss, and the pledgor could redeem by paying the remaining debt? Answer: The author answered with 'illa annahu yataqarraru bi al-halak' meaning the guarantee is not yet obligatory upon the mortgagee for this decrease because the strength of the guarantee comes from the destruction of the pawn, and the pawn is not destroyed but is alive, its value only decreased due to price drop. So the guarantee has not yet become firm. Therefore, if the pledgor redeems it in this state, he will pay the full debt. In the discussed scenario, since the pawn was destroyed by the stranger, now the full value at the day of receipt is considered (as mentioned).
Source pages p. 295

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling when a pawn is destroyed in the mortgagee's custody, whether by his act or by calamity. It first establishes the general principle: the guarantee (daman) for the pawn is based on its value at the time of receipt (qabd), not at redemption, because the mortgagee's possession is a 'qabd istifa'' (possession for collection). The guarantee becomes fixed at the moment of destruction. The text then applies this to the earlier example: the pawn's value dropped from 1000 to 500 due to a stranger's destruction; the remaining 500 price drop is treated as if destroyed in the mortgagee's hands, reducing the debt to 500. A key subtlety: if the pawn merely decreases in value without destruction (e.g., market fluctuation), the mortgagee is not liable for the decrease, and the pledgee must pay the full debt to redeem, because the guarantee only crystallizes upon destruction. This distinction is crucial in Hanafi fiqh.

Key Terms
ضمان (daman): Liability or guarantee; here it refers to the mortgagee's liability for the pawn if it is destroyed.
قبضہ استیفاء (qabd istifa'): Possession for the purpose of collecting a debt; the mortgagee's possession of the pawn is of this type.
تقرر عند الهلاك (taqarrur 'inda al-halak): The guarantee becomes fixed and determined at the time of destruction, not before.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a pawn's value drops from 1000 to 500 due to market fluctuation, but the pawn is not destroyed, how much debt must the pledgor pay to redeem it?
A) 500
B) 1000
C) 0
D) 1500

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi rahn, the mortgagee's liability for the pawn is fixed at receipt value and crystallizes only upon destruction; mere depreciation does not reduce the debt.

Mortgagee's Destruction of the Pawn: Deferred Debt and Price Drop
Rulings on mortgagee destroying pawn with deferred debt and price drop

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rules for when a mortgagee destroys a pawn, distinguishing between deferred and immediate debt and accounting for price fluctuations.

Core Idea
Destroying the pawn doesn't extinguish the debt; the value paid becomes a new pawn or offsets the debt.

This lesson addresses a common scenario in Islamic finance: if the mortgagee (lender) destroys the collateral (pawn), what happens to the debt? The Hanafi school provides clear rules: the mortgagee must pay the market value, and whether the debt is deferred or due determines how that value interacts with the debt. We also cover the situation where the value has dropped, ensuring fairness to both parties.

Guided Path
1
Identify the destruction scenario
Determine whether the debt is deferred (muajjal) or immediate, and note the value of the pawn at the time of destruction.
2
Apply liability rule for deferred debt
If the debt is deferred, the mortgagee must pay the value of the pawn at destruction; that value becomes a new pawn in his hands until the debt matures.
The substitute takes the same legal status as the original pawn.
3
Settle at maturity
When the debt matures, if the value is of the same type as the debt, the mortgagee takes his due from it; any surplus goes to the pledgor.
If the value is less, the debt is reduced by that amount.
4
Handle price drop before destruction
If the pawn's value dropped before destruction (e.g., market price reversal), the mortgagee pays the lower value at destruction, and the debt is reduced by that same amount.
The value at receipt is not used; the guarantee is based on the earlier receipt, but the amount destroyed is the actual value lost.

Source Text

ولو استهلكه المرتهن والدين مؤجل غرم القيمة لانه اتلف الغير وكانت رهنا في يده حتى يحل الدين لان الضمان بدل العين فاخذ حكمه واذا حل الدين وهو على صفة القيمة استوفى المرتهن منها قدر حقه لانه ـنس حقه ثم ان كان فيه فضل يرده على الراهن لانه بدل ملكه وقد فرغ عن حق المرتهن ترجمہ اور اگر مرہون کو مرتہن نے ہلاک کر دیا ہو اور قرض میعادی ہو تو مرتہن قیمت کا تاوان دیگا اس لئے کہ مرتہن نے غیر کی ملک کو تلف کر دیا ہے اور وہ قیمت مرتہن کے قبضہ میں رہن رہے گی۔ یہاں تک کہ ادای دین کا وقت آ جائے اس لئے کہ ضمان عین کا بدل ہے تو ضمان عین کے حکم کو لے لے گا اور جب اداء دین کا وقت آ جائے اور وہ ( قرض) قیمت کی صفت ( جنس ) پر ہے تو مرتبین قیمت سے اپنے حق کے بقدر لے لے اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے حق کی جنس ہے پھر اگر اس میں زیادتی ہو تو اس کو راہن پر واپس کر دے اس لئے کہ یہ (قیمت مرہونہ ) راہن کے حق کا بدل ہے حالانکہ یہ مرتہن کے حق سے فارغ ہو چکی ہے۔ تشریح اگر مرتہن ہی نے مرہون کو ہلاک کر دیا ہو تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ قرض میعادی ہے یا فی الحال واجب الادا ہے اگر قرض میعادی ہو تو مرتہن مرہون کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا اور وہ قیمت مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہے گی کیونکہ اگر مرہون باقی ہوتا تو اس کا بھی یہی حکم ہوتا تو اب مرہون کے بدل کا بھی یہی حکم ہوگا۔
اور مرتہن پر خنمان اس لئے واجب ہوا ہے کہ اس نے غیر کی ملک کو ضائع کر دیا ہے اور جب اداء دین کا وقت آ جائے تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ قیمت قرض کی جنس سے ہے یا نہیں تو اگر قیمت قرض کی جنس سے ہو تو اس قیمت میں سے مرتہن اپنے حق کے بقدر وصول کر لے۔ اگر اداء دین کے بعد کچھ رقم بچ جائے تو وہ راہن کو واپس دیدی جائے گی کیونکہ یہ قیمت راہن کی ملک کا بدل ہے اور اب یہ بدل مرتہن کے حق سے فارغ ہو چکا ہے تو مابقیہ راہن کو واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر قیمت قرض سے کم ہو تو اس کا حکم انگلی عبارت میں بیان کر رہے ہیں۔
مرہون کو مرتہن نے ہلاک کیا اور اس مرہون کی قیمت گھٹ گئی تومی حکم ہے
وان نقصت عن الدين بتراجع السعر الى خمس مائة وقد كانت قيمته يوم الرهن الفاوجب بالاستهلاك خمس مائة وسقط من الدين خمس مائة لأن ما انتقص كالهالك وسقط الدين بقدره وتعتبر قيمته يوم القبض وهو مضمون بالقبض السابق لا بتراجع السعر ووجب عليه الباقي بالاتلاف وهو قيمته يوم اتلف ترجمہ اور اگر قیمت قرض سے کم ہوگئی بھاؤ کے پلٹ جانے کی وجہ سے پانچ سو تک حالانکہ اس کی قیمت رہن کے دن ہزار تھی تو ہلاک کرنے کی وجہ سے پانچ سو واجب ہوں گے اور قرض میں سے پانچ سو ساقط ہوں گے اس لئے کہ ( قیمت کی ) جو مقدار گھٹ گئی
If the mortgagee destroys the pawn and the debt is deferred, what is the ruling? And if the mortgagee destroys it and the debt is deferred, he pays the value because he destroyed the property of another, and it remains as a pawn in his hand until the debt matures, because the guarantee is the substitute for the property, so it takes its ruling. And when the debt matures and it is of the same type as the value, the mortgagee takes from it the amount of his right because it is the genus of his right. Then if there is surplus, he returns it to the pledgor because it is the substitute for his property and has been freed from the mortgagee's right. Translation: And if the mortgagee has destroyed the pawn and the debt is deferred, then the mortgagee will pay compensation of the value, because he has destroyed the property of another, and that value will remain as a pawn in his possession until the time of payment of the debt, because the guarantee is the substitute for the property, so it will take the ruling of the property. When the time of payment comes and it (the debt) is of the same type as the value, the mortgagee takes from the value the amount of his right because it is the genus of his right. Then if there is surplus, he returns it to the pledgor because it (the value) is the substitute for the pledgor's property and has become free from the mortgagee's right. Explanation: If the mortgagee himself destroys the pawn, then we see whether the debt is deferred or presently due. If the debt is deferred, the mortgagee is liable for the value of the pawn, and that value remains as a pawn with the mortgagee, because if the pawn had remained, its ruling would be the same; so now the substitute takes the same ruling. The mortgagee became liable because he wasted the property of another. When the time of payment comes, we see whether the value is of the same type as the debt. If yes, the mortgagee takes from it the amount of his right. If after payment some amount remains, it is returned to the pledgor, because this value is the substitute for the pledgor's property and has become free from the mortgagee's right. But if the value is less than the debt, its ruling is being explained in the following phrase. 
If the mortgagee destroys the pawn and its value has decreased, what is the ruling? And if it decreased from the debt due to a reversal of price to five hundred, while its value on the day of pledge was one thousand, then due to the destruction, five hundred is obligatory and from the debt five hundred is dropped, because what decreased is like destroyed, and the debt drops by its amount. And its value on the day of receipt is considered, and it is guaranteed by the earlier receipt, not by the reversal of price, and the remainder is obligatory upon him due to destruction, and that is its value on the day he destroyed it.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This lesson contains two rulings. The first ruling: if the mortgagee (murtahin) destroys the pawn (marhun) and the debt is deferred (muajjal), the mortgagee must pay the value of the pawn at the time of destruction. This value becomes a new pawn in his hands until the debt matures. When the debt matures, if the value is of the same type as the debt, the mortgagee can take his due from it; any surplus goes to the pledgor (rahin). This is because the value substitutes for the original pawn. The second ruling: if the value of the pawn has dropped before destruction (e.g., from 1000 to 500 due to market reversal), and the mortgagee destroys it, he pays the lower value (500) and the debt is reduced by that amount (500). The basis is the value at the time of receipt (qabd), not the drop in price, and the amount destroyed is considered as if it were the pawn. The remaining debt drops proportionally.

Key Terms
دین مؤجل (dayn muajjal): A debt that is due at a future date, not immediately payable.
بدل عین (badal al-'ayn): The substitute for a specific property; here the value paid by the mortgagee stands in place of the pawn.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; here the mortgagee is liable for the value of the pawn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If the mortgagee destroys a pawn worth 1000 at receipt but only 500 at destruction (due to market drop), and the debt is 1000, how much debt is extinguished?
A) 1000
B) 500
C) 0
D) 1500

Key Takeaway
The mortgagee's destruction does not cancel the debt; the value paid stands in for the pawn and is treated similarly, and if value dropped, only the dropped value offsets the debt.

Ruling When the Murtahin Destroys the Marhun with a Deferred Debt
States ruling for murtahin destroying marhun with deferred debt

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when the murtahin destroys the marhun while the debt is deferred, and explain the reasoning behind the substitution of the value as a new pledge.

Core Idea
If the murtahin destroys the marhun, the value becomes a new pledge until the deferred debt matures.

In a mortgage (rahn) contract, the murtahin holds the marhun as security. If the murtahin himself destroys the marhun, the debt remains outstanding. This lesson examines the specific ruling when the debt is deferred (mu'ajjal): the murtahin must pay the value, which then stands in place of the original asset as a pledge. We will unpack the legal reasoning and the practical steps upon maturity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario
We have a valid rahn contract with a deferred debt. The murtahin (creditor) destroys the marhun (pledged property).
The destruction is by the murtahin's own act; this triggers liability.
2
Understand the immediate ruling
The murtahin must pay the value (qimah) of the marhun on the day he took possession. This value is not a repayment of the debt but a substitute for the destroyed asset.
The value becomes a new pledge in the murtahin's hands until the debt matures.
3
Trace the legal reasoning (ta'lil)
The guarantee (daman) is a substitute for the property (badal al-'ayn). Therefore, the value inherits the same ruling as the original marhun: it remains as collateral.
The murtahin's liability arises from causing loss to another's property (itlaf al-ghayr).
4
Determine the process upon debt maturity
When the debt becomes due, if the value is of the same genus as the debt, the murtahin recovers his right from the value. Any surplus is returned to the rahin.
If the value is less than the debt, the ruling is covered in the next section.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہون کو مرتہن ہلاک کر دے اور دین مؤجل ہو تو کیا حکم ہے
ولو استهلكه المرتهن والدين مؤجل غرم القيمة لانه اتلف الغير وكانت رهنا في يده حتى يحل الدين لان الضمان بدل العين فاخذ حكمه واذا حل الدين وهو على صفة القيمة استوفى المرتهن منها قدر حقه لانه جنس حقه ثم ان كان فيه فضل يرده على الراهن لانه بدل ملكه وقد فرغ عن حق المرتهن
ترجمہ اور اگر مرہون کو مرتہن نے ہلاک کر دیا ہو اور قرض میعادی ہو تو مرتہن قیمت کا تاوان دیگا اس لئے کہ مرتہن نے غیر کی ملک کو تلف کر دیا ہے اور وہ قیمت مرتہن کے قبضہ میں رہن رہے گی۔ یہاں تک کہ ادای دین کا وقت آ جائے اس لئے کہ ضمان عین کا بدل ہے تو ضمان عین کے حکم کو لے لے گا اور جب اداء دین کا وقت آ جائے اور وہ ( قرض) قیمت کی صفت ( جنس ) پر ہے تو مرتبین قیمت سے اپنے حق کے بقدر لے لے اس لئے کہ یہ اس کے حق کی جنس ہے پھر اگر اس میں زیادتی ہو تو اس کو راہن پر واپس کر دے اس لئے کہ یہ (قیمت مرہونہ ) راہن کے حق کا بدل ہے حالانکہ یہ مرتہن کے حق سے فارغ ہو چکی ہے۔
تشریح اگر مرتہن ہی نے مرہون کو ہلاک کر دیا ہو تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ قرض میعادی ہے یا فی الحال واجب الادا ہے اگر قرض میعادی ہو تو مرتہن مرہون کی قیمت کا ضامن ہوگا اور وہ قیمت مرتہن کے پاس رہن رہے گی کیونکہ اگر مرہون باقی ہوتا تو اس کا بھی یہی حکم ہوتا تو اب مرہون کے بدل کا بھی یہی حکم ہوگا۔ اور مرتہن پر ضمان اس لئے واجب ہوا ہے کہ اس نے غیر کی ملک کو ضائع کر دیا ہے اور جب اداء دین کا وقت آ جائے تو اب دیکھا جائے کہ قیمت قرض کی جنس سے ہے یا نہیں تو اگر قیمت قرض کی جنس سے ہو تو اس قیمت میں سے مرتہن اپنے حق کے بقدر وصول کر لے۔ اگر اداء دین کے بعد کچھ رقم بچ جائے تو وہ راہن کو واپس دیدی جائے گی کیونکہ یہ قیمت راہن کی ملک کا بدل ہے اور اب یہ بدل مرتہن کے حق سے فارغ ہو چکا ہے تو مابقیہ راہن کو واپس کر دیا جائے گا۔ لیکن اگر قیمت قرض سے کم ہو تو اس کا حکم انگلی عبارت میں بیان کر رہے ہیں۔
What is the ruling if the murtahin destroys the marhun and the debt is deferred? And if the murtahin destroys it and the debt is deferred, he must pay the value, because he destroyed the property of another, and it (the value) remains a pledge in his hand until the debt becomes due, because the guarantee is a substitute for the property, so it takes its ruling. And when the debt becomes due and it (the debt) is of the same category as the value, the murtahin recovers from it the amount of his right, because it is of the same genus as his right. Then if there is a surplus, he returns it to the rahin, because it is the substitute for his property and has been released from the right of the murtahin. Translation: And if the murtahin has destroyed the marhun and the debt is deferred, the murtahin must pay compensation of the value, because he has destroyed the property of another, and that value will remain as a pledge in the possession of the murtahin until the time of payment of the debt arrives, because the guarantee is a substitute for the property, so it takes the ruling of the guarantee of the property. And when the time for payment arrives and the debt is of the same category as the value, the murtahin takes from the value the amount of his right, because this is of the same genus as his right. Then if there is an excess in it, he returns it to the rahin, because this value is a substitute for the property of the rahin, and it has been released from the right of the murtahin. Explanation: If the murtahin himself destroyed the marhun, then it is seen whether the debt is deferred or immediately payable. If the debt is deferred, the murtahin is liable for the value of the marhun, and that value will remain as a pledge with the murtahin, because if the marhun had remained, its ruling would have been the same, so now the substitute of the marhun will have the same ruling. And the guarantee is obligatory on the murtahin because he destroyed the property of another. And when the time for payment arrives, it is seen whether the value is of the same category as the debt or not. If the value is of the same category as the debt, then the murtahin recovers from this value the amount of his right. If after payment some amount remains, it will be returned to the rahin, because this value is the substitute for the property of the rahin, and now this substitute is free from the right of the murtahin, so the remainder will be returned to the rahin. But if the value is less than the debt, its ruling will be stated in the following expression.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the Hidayah on the case where the murtahin (mortgagee) destroys the marhun (pledged property) while the debt is deferred (mu'ajjal). The ruling is that the murtahin must pay the value (qimah) of the marhun on the day he took possession (yaum al-qabd). This value then takes the place of the original marhun as a new pledge (marhun) in the hands of the murtahin until the debt becomes due. This is because the guarantee (daman) is a substitute (badal) for the property ('ayn), so it inherits the same ruling. When the debt becomes due, if the debt is of the same genus (jins) as the value (i.e., same currency), the murtahin can take from the value an amount equal to his right (his debt). If there is a surplus (fadl), he must return it to the rahin (pledgor) because the value is now the substitute for the rahin's property and is free from the murtahin's right. If the value is less than the debt, the deficiency will be addressed in the next section. The commentary (tafsir) clarifies that the liability (daman) is incurred because the murtahin caused loss to another's property (itlaf al-ghayr). The passage is purely statement of ruling without explicit scriptural proof; it is based on established Hanafi principles of substitution (badal al-'ayn).

Key Terms
مرتهن (murtahin): The mortgagee; the creditor who takes possession of the pledged property as security for the debt.
مرهون (marhun): The pledged property; the asset given as collateral for a debt.
ضمان (daman): Guarantee or liability; here refers to the murtahin's responsibility for the marhun and the obligation to pay its value if destroyed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What happens to the value paid by the murtahin when he destroys the marhun and the debt is deferred?
A) It is given to the rahin immediately as compensation.
B) It becomes a new pledge (marhun) in the hands of the murtahin until the debt is due.
C) It is used to immediately reduce the debt.
D) The murtahin keeps it as his own property.

Key Takeaway
When the murtahin destroys the marhun with a deferred debt, the value substitutes as a pledge; the debt remains, and upon maturity, the murtahin recovers his due and returns the surplus.

Destroying a Pledged Item After Market Decline: Two Guarantees
Ruling on murtahin's destruction after market decline

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling when a pledged item (marhun) is destroyed by the pledgee (murtahin) after its market value has decreased, and calculate the resulting reduction in debt.

Core Idea
The murtahin guarantees the value at possession, not later price; the price drop reduces the debt.

We continue examining the murtahin's liability when destroying the marhun. In the previous lesson, the marhun was worth what it was at the time of destruction. Here, a new factor enters: the market value has dropped before destruction. How does this affect the debt and compensation? The Hanafi school introduces two distinct guarantees: one for possession (daman al-istiblaq) and one for the loss due to destruction (daman al-itlaf). Understanding this distinction is essential for accurate application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of guarantee
The murtahin is liable for the marhun due to possession (qabd). This is daman al-istiblaq — the guarantee of possession. Additionally, when he destroys it, he incurs daman al-itlaf (guarantee of destruction). In this scenario, the value has dropped, so part of the destruction is the loss from the price decline.
The loss due to price drop is treated as part of the destroyed value.
2
Determine the value for each guarantee
For daman al-istiblaq, the relevant value is the value at the time of possession (yaum al-qabd). For daman al-itlaf, the value is the value at the time of destruction (yaum al-itlaf). In the example: possession value = 1000, destruction value = 500.
The price drop does not affect the possession guarantee.
3
Calculate the effect on the debt
The loss from the price drop (500) is treated as destroyed — it reduces the debt by that amount. The murtahin must also pay the value at possession (1000) as a new pledge? Actually, the commentary says he must pay 500 (the destruction value) as compensation for the loss, and this 500 is kept as a pledge. The debt is reduced by 500. So net: the murtahin now has a new pledge of 500 against a remaining debt of 500.
Key: the loss reduces the debt; the murtahin does not get double liability.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مرہون کو مرتہن نے ہلاک کیا اور اس مرہون کی قیمت گھٹ گئی تو کیا حکم ہے
وان نقصت عن الدين بتراجع السعر الى خمس مائة وقد كانت قيمته يوم الرهن الفاوجب بالاستهلاك خمس مائة وسقط من الدين خمس مائة لأن ما انتقص كالهالك وسقط الدين بقدره وتعتبر قيمته يوم القبض وهو مضمون بالقبض السابق لا بتراجع السعر ووجب عليه الباقي بالاتلاف وهو قيمته يوم اتلف
ترجمہ اور اگر قیمت قرض سے کم ہوگئی بھاؤ کے پلٹ جانے کی وجہ سے پانچ سو تک حالانکہ اس کی قیمت رہن کے دن ہزار تھی تو ہلاک کرنے کی وجہ سے پانچ سو واجب ہوں گے اور قرض میں سے پانچ سو ساقط ہوں گے اس لئے کہ ( قیمت کی ) جو مقدار گھٹ گئی وہ مالک کے مثل ہے اور ہا لک کے بقدر قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا اور اس کے قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی اور مرتہن پر مرہون سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہے بھاؤ کے پلٹنے کی وجہ سے نہیں اور مرتہن پر باقی اتلاف کی وجہ سے واجب ہوگا اور وہ مرہون کی یوم تلف کی قیمت ہے۔
تشریح جس مرہون کو مرتہن نے ہلاک کیا ہے اگر اس کی قیمت گھٹ گئی تو کیا حکم ہے؟ تو فرمایا کہ اس کمی کا ضمان مرتہن پر پڑیگا۔ جس کی تفصیل یہ ہے کہ جس دن رہن رکھا گیا اس دن کی قیمت ہزار روپے ہیں پھر بھاؤ کے الٹ پھیر سے مرہون کی قیمت پانچ سو روپے رہ گئی اب مرتہن نے اس کو ہلاک کر دیا تو مرتہن پر دو ضمان ہوئے ایک تو ضمان استبلاک اور دوسرا ضمان نقصان لہذا ضمان استبلاک کی وجہ سے مرتہن پر پانچ سو روپے عربوں کی قیمت کے لازم ہوں گے جس کو رہن رکھدیا جائے گا اور نقصان کے پانچ سوروپے کی وجہ سے مرتہن کے قرض میں سے پانچ سوروپے ساقط ہو کر اب صرف پانچ سورہ گئے ۔ کیونکہ جب مرہون ہلاک ہو جائے اس وقت نقصان بھی مضمون ہوتا ہے ( کما مر ) لہذ ا نقصان کو ہلاکت کا درجہ دیا جائے گا اور مقدار نقصان قرض ساقط ہو جائے گا۔ اور چونکہ مرہون سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے مرتبہن کی زیر ضمانت داخل ہے لہذا یوم قبضہ کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی ۔ لا بستر اجع السعر الخ یعنی مرہون مرتہن کے زیر ضمان بھاؤ کی الٹ پھیر کی وجہ سے داخل نہیں ہوا بلکہ سابق قبضہ کی وجہ سے مضمون ہے تو قبضہ کے دن کی قیمت مضمون ہو گی ۔ اور جو پانچ سو روپے کا ضمان واجب ہوا ہے وہ اختلاف کی وجہ سے واجب ہوا ہے تو اس میں یوم تلف کی قیمت معتبر ہوگی ۔
What is the ruling if the murtahin destroyed the marhun and its value decreased? And if it decreased from the debt due to a drop in price to five hundred, while its value on the day of pledge was one thousand, then due to the destruction five hundred is obligatory, and from the debt five hundred is cancelled, because whatever decreased is like the destroyed, and the debt is cancelled by its amount. And its value on the day of possession is considered, and it is guaranteed by the prior possession, not by the drop in price. And the remainder is obligatory upon him due to destruction, and it is its value on the day he destroyed it. Translation: And if the value became less than the debt due to the reversal of price to five hundred, while its value on the day of pledge was one thousand, then due to destruction five hundred becomes obligatory, and from the debt five hundred is dropped, because the amount that decreased is like the destroyed, and the debt is dropped by its amount. And the value on the day of possession is considered, and the marhun is guaranteed on the murtahin due to prior possession, not due to price reversal. And the remainder is obligatory on him due to destruction, and that is its value on the day of destruction. Explanation: Regarding the marhun which the murtahin destroyed, if its value decreased, what is the ruling? He said that the guarantee of this decrease falls on the murtahin. The detail is that on the day the pledge was given, its value was one thousand rupees. Then, due to market fluctuation, the value of the marhun became five hundred rupees. Now the murtahin destroyed it. So two guarantees apply to the murtahin: one is the guarantee of possession (daman al-istiblaq) and the other is the guarantee of loss (daman al-nuqsan). Therefore, due to the guarantee of possession, five hundred rupees becomes obligatory on the murtahin, which will be kept as a pledge. And due to the five hundred rupees of loss, five hundred rupees from the murtahin's debt is cancelled, so now only five hundred remain. Because when the marhun is destroyed, the loss is also guaranteed (as mentioned earlier), so the loss is given the status of destruction, and the amount of loss reduces the debt. And since the marhun is included in the murtahin's guarantee due to prior possession, the value on the day of possession is considered. 'Not due to price reversal' means the marhun did not come under the murtahin's guarantee due to price fluctuation, but is guaranteed due to prior possession, so the value on the day of possession is what is guaranteed. And the five hundred rupees that became obligatory due to destruction (by himself?) - there the value on the day of destruction is considered.
Source pages p. 296

Commentary
This passage continues the ruling on murtahin destroying the marhun, but now with the scenario where the market value of the marhun has decreased before the destruction. The rahin pledged an item worth 1000 at the time of contract. Later, due to market downturn, its value drops to 500. The murtahin then destroys it. The ruling distinguishes between two components: (1) The value at the time of possession (yaum al-qabd) which is 1000 - this is the value for which the murtahin is liable as a guarantee (daman) due to his prior possession (qabd al-sabiq). This is called daman al-istiblaq. So he must pay 500 (the current value? Wait: the commentary says 500 is wajib due to daman al-istiblaq - but that seems contradictory. Let's read carefully: The Arabic matn says: وان نقصت عن الدين بتراجع السعر الى خمس مائة وقد كانت قيمته يوم الرهن الفاوجب بالاستهلاك خمس مائة وسقط من الدين خمس مائة. 'And if it decreased from the debt due to price drop to five hundred, while its value on the day of pledge was one thousand, then due to destruction five hundred is obligatory and from the debt five hundred is cancelled.' The commentary explains that two guarantees apply: one for the value at time of possession (1000) and one for the loss. But actually, the ruling is: The murtahin must pay the value at the time of destruction (yaum atlaf) for the part that was destroyed? Wait, the Arabic: 'ووجب عليه الباقي بالاتلاف وهو قيمته يوم اتلف' - the remainder (the part exceeding the debt reduction?) is obligatory due to destruction and it is its value on the day he destroyed it. The commentary says: the 500 that is wajib due to istiblaq will be kept as pledge, and the 500 loss reduces the debt. So net, the murtahin pays nothing extra? The debt was originally, say, 1000? The debt amount is not specified, but if the marhun was worth 1000 at pledge, and the debt is also 1000, then after decrease to 500, if murtahin destroys it, he must pay 500 (value at destruction?) which becomes new pledge, and the debt reduces by 500 to 500. So murtahin still owes 500. But the commentary says the 500 from istiblaq is kept as pledge, and the 500 loss reduces debt. So end result: murtahin holds 500 as new pledge against 500 debt. That seems consistent. The key principle: the murtahin's liability for the value at time of possession covers the base guarantee; the loss due to price drop is treated as part of the destruction and reduces the debt proportionally. The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah as it is from Hidayah.

Key Terms
تراجع السعر (taraju' al-si'r): Market price decrease; drop in the market value of the marhun.
ضمان استبلاک (daman al-istiblaq): The liability incurred due to possession; the murtahin's guarantee of the marhun by virtue of taking possession.
ضمان نقصان (daman al-nuqsan): Guarantee for the loss in value; the part of the destruction attributed to the price drop.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a marhun is destroyed by the murtahin after its market value has dropped, what happens to the debt?
A) The debt remains unchanged.
B) The debt is reduced by the amount of the loss in value.
C) The debt is fully cancelled.
D) The debt is increased by the amount of the loss.

Key Takeaway
When a pledged item is destroyed after a market decline, the murtahin's possession guarantee anchors the value, and the loss reduces the debt accordingly.
